Ministry of Industry and Commerce - Commodity Inspection Bureau - Schedules Livestock Inspection - Effective August 1 122

In recent years, diseases that our country has never experienced before have been introduced from foreign countries, spreading in the mainland and causing great harm. The Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, in order to prevent their introduction and spread, is conducting import inspection of livestock. Preparations were previously ordered, and draft implementing rules and supplementary measures for the inspection were submitted to the ministry and then to the Executive Yuan for approval and promulgation. It has now been decided to first implement the inspection of imported cattle and sheep, effective August 1. Cattle and sheep that are not inspected and qualified will not be allowed to be declared for import. The details are as follows:

Compilation of Notices: The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce and the Jianghai Customs have both issued notices separately regarding the implementation of livestock inspection as ordered. (1) The notice from the Commodity Inspection Bureau states: "This Bureau has decided to implement the inspection of imported livestock as of August 1, as ordered. Cattle and sheep imported through Shanghai that have not been inspected and approved by this Bureau will not be allowed to be declared for import. In addition to distributing the implementing rules and supplementary measures, this notice is hereby promulgated for general knowledge." Signed, Cai Wuji, Director. (2) The Jianghai Customs notice states: "In accordance with the government's order, all livestock (cattle, buffalo, sheep, goats) imported from foreign countries should first be inspected by the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce before being allowed to be imported, etc. In accordance with this order, it is now determined to be implemented from August 1 of this year. All detailed measures can be inquired at this Customs Office. All merchants should be aware of this. Special notice." Signed, Tang Haian, Superintendent; Lofede, Customs Commissioner.

Implementing Rules: Article 1: These rules are formulated in accordance with Article 18 of the Commodity Inspection Law (hereinafter referred to as the Law). Article 2: The livestock referred to in these rules refers to chickens, ducks, geese, turkeys, and other poultry; and cattle, sheep, horses, pigs, dogs, cats, camels, and other livestock; as well as wild animals closely related to poultry and livestock. The types of livestock listed in the preceding paragraph that should be inspected, and their locations, will be determined separately by ministerial order. Article 3: All livestock imported from foreign countries must submit an inspection application form to the local Commodity Inspection Bureau (hereinafter referred to as the Inspection Bureau) twenty-four hours before import, together with the inspection fee, and apply for inspection. Article 4: All livestock imported from foreign countries may be required to submit an inspection certificate issued by the veterinary office of the government of the area of origin or the place of export of the country of origin, if necessary. The inspection certificate in the preceding paragraph must state the following items: (A) the name of the area of origin or the place of export of the country of origin of the livestock, and that there have been no outbreaks of various infectious diseases listed in Article 10 of these rules within sixty days before shipment; (B) the species, breed, shape, markings, age, sex of each livestock, and the date and results of various diagnostic examinations before shipment. Article 5: When imported livestock arrive at the port, the Inspection Bureau will send personnel to the ship or other designated location to conduct inspection. If the livestock has the certificate stipulated in the preceding article and is confirmed to be healthy and disease-free after inspection, an inspection certificate will be issued and allowed to be released. Article 6: If imported livestock has any of the following conditions, it shall be transported to the designated isolation center under the direction of the Inspection Bureau for isolation diagnosis: (1) not having an inspection certificate issued by the veterinary office of the government of the area of origin or the place of export of the country of origin; (2) the inspection finds that it does not match the description in the submitted certificate; (3) the inspection finds that it has an infectious disease or is suspected of having an infectious disease. Article 7: The period of stay of imported livestock in the designated isolation center shall be determined by the Inspection Bureau. Personnel and items related to the livestock must be permitted by the Inspection Bureau before being allowed to pass or be carried in. Article 8: During the period of stay of imported livestock in the isolation center, the Inspection Bureau must conduct various necessary diagnoses of contact infectious diseases and parasitic pests. The diseases that should be diagnosed will be determined by the Inspection Bureau. For the various diagnoses in the preceding paragraph, the Inspection Bureau may charge a diagnostic fee, and the amount of the fee will be determined separately by the Inspection Bureau. Article 9: Imported livestock that have completed the stay period in the isolation center and pass the inspection will be issued an inspection certificate and allowed to be released. Article 10: If livestock imported from foreign countries is found by the Inspection Bureau to have bovine contagious pleuropneumonia, contagious abortion disease, Malta fever, tuberculosis, foot-and-mouth disease, surra, anthrax, redwater fever, rinderpest, swine erysipelas, hog cholera, swine pneumonia, glanders, epizootic lymphangitis, equine syphilis, equine strangles, epizootic and ulcerative lymphangitis, rabies, fowl cholera, fowl diphtheria, fowl plague, fowl typhoid, and other contact infectious diseases or parasitic pests, the Inspection Bureau will order treatment as appropriate, or directly slaughter, burn, or bury them. No compensation will be given for all losses. Article 11: The transportation costs of imported livestock to the isolation center, and all food costs, management fees, transportation fees, medical expenses, etc. during the stay period, shall be borne by the applicant. Article 12: If imported livestock suffers from common diseases while staying in the isolation center, the applicant may hire a veterinarian for diagnosis and treatment. The applicant shall be solely responsible for any losses due to death from illness or other accidents. Article 13: The Inspection Bureau may formulate supplementary measures for the implementation of livestock inspection, but must submit them to the Ministry for record. Article 14: These rules shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

Supplementary Measures: Article 1: Cattle and sheep imported from foreign countries may obtain a customs declaration voucher at the time of application. The customs declaration voucher in the preceding paragraph is divided into three copies. In addition to the first copy being kept by the Bureau, the first copy is used to obtain the certificate, and the third copy is submitted to the customs for verification, all of which are delivered to the applicant for use. Article 2: When cattle or sheep are imported, in accordance with the provisions of Article 4 of the rules, when ordered to submit various certificates issued by foreign government veterinarians, a tuberculosis inspection certificate, a contagious abortion disease inspection certificate, a Malta fever inspection certificate, and a bovine contagious pleuropneumonia inspection certificate should also be submitted. Article 3: During the period of stay of cattle or sheep in the isolation center, at least one test for contagious abortion disease, a test for tuberculosis, a test for surra, a test for Malta fever, and a test for bovine contagious pleuropneumonia must be performed. Any animal with contagious abortion disease, surra, Malta fever, or bovine contagious pleuropneumonia will be slaughtered and burned or buried. Article 4: The period of stay of cattle or sheep in the designated isolation center must be at least fifteen days. Milk products and young animals produced during the stay period must obtain the permission of the Inspection Bureau before being allowed to be taken out of the center. Article 5: In accordance with the provisions of Article 8 of the rules, the amount of the diagnosis fee for cattle or goats is stipulated as follows: Diagnosis fee for cattle: 10 National currency for the first head, with an additional fee of 2 yuan for each additional head. Diagnosis fee for goats: 1 yuan for the first head, with an additional fee of 50 cents for each additional head. Article 6: Those who purchase cattle or sheep from foreign countries should register before purchasing. Article 7: These measures will be implemented from the date of promulgation by bureau order after being submitted to the Ministry for approval and record.

Starting with Cattle and Sheep: The Commodity Inspection Bureau has decided to formally implement the inspection starting from August 1, starting with the inspection of cattle and sheep. After obtaining effective results, other livestock will be inspected. At present, if animal diseases are discovered, they will be sent to the Jiangwan Animal Disease Isolation Center to avoid transmission. All inspection personnel have also been appointed, including Li Yangshan, Chen Shaojiong, Yang Genrong, Peng Zhongxin, Chen Zilong, Yang Xingye, and Xu Yusheng, totaling seven people, and the livestock group director of the Bureau, Chen Shunyun, is responsible.

Takahashi Seaside Bathing Resort Grand Event: Xingye Society Hosted Over 200 Chinese and Western Guests Yesterday 124

The Takahashi Seaside Bathing Resort, this year taken back by the Municipal Government and handed over to the Xingye Trust Company for management, has been extensively renovated and refurbished by the company. Since its opening, it has attracted a considerable number of visitors. Yesterday, the company invited reporters from various Chinese and Western newspapers in Shanghai and personnel from various shipping companies to visit. The details are as follows:

A Glimpse Along the Way: Yesterday, over two hundred Chinese and foreign news reporters and personnel from various shipping companies, led by the company's General Manager Xu Fu, Manager Tan Boying, Deputy Manager Zhou Xin, and other staff members, were warmly received. A newly built No. 6 wave-breaking ferry was specially prepared for the guests. The structure and equipment of this ferry are generally similar to the No. 5 ferry, but its materials are more robust and its decoration is more luxurious than the No. 5 ferry. Its top speed can reach thirteen nautical miles, surpassing all other ferries. At 2:30 PM, the ferry departed from the Beijing Road Pier. As soon as it set sail, a refreshing coolness was immediately felt, and the sweltering heat completely dissipated. No wonder the night ferries are crowded with people seeking relief from the heat. Even in the hottest weather, when there is not even a slight breeze in gardens or open fields, a cool breeze naturally arises as soon as the ferry sets sail. After passing Qingning Temple, the air became even clearer. The fields on both sides were boundless and green, and the sandpipers and sailboats created a picturesque scene. The reporters either tapped on the railings and sang loudly or sat around chatting, full of interest. After about an hour, they arrived at Takahashi, where ten buses were already lined up at the pier waiting. These vehicles had large bodies, freshly painted, and unusually comfortable spring seats. The road was also smoother than in previous years. In about ten minutes, they reached the bathing resort.

A Tour of the Bathing Resort: After entering the resort, they first visited it separately. The structure of the buildings in the resort is quite unique, with green tile roofs, whitewashed walls, and supporting vermilion pillars, creating a dazzling array of colors. At the north end are two large dressing rooms for men and women, each with clothing lockers, changing rooms, shower rooms, and the like. Male and female staff members separately rent out various swimming supplies, bathrobes, towels, and other items. In the middle is the office, and at the south end is the dining hall, which is a branch of the Lakeside Restaurant, selling high-quality Western dishes and famous Yangzhou snacks. In front of the dining hall is a large lawn, also filled with tables and chairs for guests to dine. Next to the lawn is a Mongolian yurt, with a cold drink stand inside, selling various cold drinks for tourists to purchase nearby. Short stools are arranged in three circles around the cold drink stand for tourists to rest. Further south is the tent rental area, with hundreds of tents available for rent. Behind the tents is a grassy area of several acres, covering more than 300 square meters, with green turf like a carpet. After bathing in the sea, tourists often come to the lawn for sunbathing. Behind the lawn are cool houses where people can stay. In addition, there are several pavilions for resting. At that time, many tourists were already swimming in the sea. The beach here is shallow and flat, making it a very suitable seaside bathing resort. Now, with the addition of modern facilities and scientific management, arranged in an orderly manner, it can add another glorious page to the history of municipal construction. After the tour, the receptionists politely led the guests into the dining hall for refreshments. The refreshments were homemade by the Lakeside Restaurant, both Chinese and Western, exquisite and delicious. Some of the guests who enjoyed swimming changed clothes and entered the water for swimming and bathing. Around 5 PM, they all boarded the original ship and returned to Shanghai, arriving when the city was already illuminated by thousands of lights.

Additional Notes on the Trip: To facilitate visits to Takahashi Seaside Bathing Resort by employed people on non-holidays, the Municipal Ferry has added special return trips every day. "Outbound" ferries depart every hour from 7 AM to 7 PM, departing from the Beijing Road Pier on the hour. "Return" trips, in addition to the original schedule, will also include a special return trip from Takahashi at 10 PM, arriving at the Beijing Road Pier at 11 PM, or taking the cool night ferry, arriving in Shanghai at 12:30 AM, rain or shine.

Wu Xixiang and Others Accuse of Embezzling Twelve Million: Continued Hearing Yesterday; Defendant Files Counterclaim; Judge Orders Witness Deng Junxiang to Court 127

Wu Xixiang, Xisi, Xixun, and Xiliu, four brothers from Anhui, residing at No. 22 Puqing Lane, Malong Road, French Concession, are the sons of the late Wu Fuqing, chief accountant of the Shanghai HSBC Bank. Recently, they hired lawyers Zhang Shizhao and Peng Yuanxun to file a complaint with the Criminal Court of the Second Special Court, accusing their cousin Wu Hengsun, son of Wu Youling, former comprador of the Beiping HSBC Bank, residing at No. 4, Lane 159, Haig Road, of embezzling

Partnership Business: Earnings and family property during his tenure as a comprador of the Beiping HSBC Bank, amounting to twelve million taels. After a preliminary hearing, the court adjourned and scheduled another hearing because the defendant did not appear. The plaintiffs’ intentions have already been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Judge Qiu Huaning of the Second Special Court again opened the Second Criminal Court for a continued hearing. Apart from Wu Xixiang, who did not appear, Xisi, Xixun, and Xiliu, along with the defendant Wu Hengsun, each arrived with their lawyers. After first questioning both parties regarding their age and residence, the court ordered the plaintiff Wu Xixun to state the main points of the indictment. He briefly stated that the former Beiping HSBC Bank

Comprador Position: Was nominally held by the defendant's father, Youling, but was actually a partnership business operated by the three families within the family, and they had not yet separated. After the death of their father, Fuqing, the defendant's side stopped paying the allowance. In May of the previous year, they negotiated with the defendant, but mediation by relatives and friends failed to reach a satisfactory resolution. Asked whether there was a partnership agreement at the time, he replied, no. The court then issued a copy of the defendant's counterclaim accusing them of false accusations to the plaintiffs in court. At this point, the defendant's lawyer stood up and stated that, regardless of the facts, from a legal point of view,

There Was Absolutely No Basis: (1) The defendant's father had been dead for eighteen years, and the statute of limitations for pursuing the right to prosecute expires within ten years. (2) The plaintiffs and the defendant are blood relatives within the fifth degree of kinship. If there was embezzlement, it would be a crime that requires a complaint to be made. The plaintiffs had already hired a lawyer to negotiate in May of the previous year, as evidenced by letters. Now, two years have passed, and the plaintiffs should have filed a lawsuit within six months, but the time has passed. (3) The facts of the dispute occurred in Beiping, and according to Article 4 of the Shanghai French Concession Court Establishment Agreement, the

Jurisdiction Is Incorrect: (4) The dispute involves events that occurred over eighteen years ago and have been subject to several general amnesties, so the court should order a dismissal. (5) Regardless of whether the defendant's father had an agreement with the plaintiffs' father to operate a comprador business but did not distribute the profits, the plaintiffs would be mistaken in their claim, as the father's liabilities cannot be inherited by his son. He requested the court to rule for dismissal or non-acceptance. Then, Zhang Shizhao, the lawyer representing the plaintiffs, stood up and

Responded to Each Point: After that, the court questioned the plaintiff Wu Xixun and Deng Junxiang about when they succeeded as compradors. Wu replied that he succeeded after the death of the defendant's father, but he could not remember the year. The court then questioned the defendant Wu Hengsun, who testified that his ancestors fled from Anhui to Jiangsu during the Taiping Rebellion and had no family property. They each made a living on their own. The comprador position at the Beiping HSBC Bank was solely operated by his father for twenty years, with an annual surplus of about 20,000 gold pieces, which also had to be distributed to colleagues. He provided some relief and assistance to the plaintiffs' side when they were in need, but it was not a fixed amount each year. As for the claim of twelve million,

The Difference Is Too Great: The plaintiff Wu Xixun also stated to the court that when his father celebrated his eightieth birthday, his cousin Youling came to Shanghai to offer his congratulations. His father asked him for twelve million, and he said that he only had six million. The judge said that everyone was dead, and it was useless to say that. Now, the defendant has filed a counterclaim accusing them of false accusations. Wu replied that they were stating the facts. At this point, the plaintiffs' lawyer presented two old-fashioned red letters as evidence, stating that the defendant's father had once mentioned in the letters that he had stored funds on their behalf. At this point, Judge Qiu ordered the plaintiffs to invite the witness Deng Junxiang (currently residing in Suzhou) to court to testify and informed the defendant that the counterclaim would be accepted. The hearing was adjourned to 10:00 AM on August 8th, and the court announced the adjournment.

Regarding the documents contained in the previous year's annual publication, it was agreed that this year's document proposal should be combined with the 25th-year printing. (2) Regarding a small number of members who owed membership fees, it was resolved to urge them to come to the association to pay. Otherwise, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce would be asked to collect the fees according to the law. (3) How to handle the aviation donation was discussed and resolved. The aviation donation of several tens of yuan was collected and sent immediately in order to conclude the matter. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

Qiu Gubiao Commits Suicide by Poisoning 138

Qiu Gubiao, a native of Ningbo, was 28 years old. He had been working as a tea server at the Dakang Gold Exchange, a brokerage firm run by his fellow townsman Wang Ziting (resident of No. 28 Qingyun Lane, Raul Dong Road, French Concession) on Second Horse Road. Recently, Wang's business suffered losses, and the firm closed down, so Qiu was serving in Wang's household. Suddenly, on the evening of the 25th at 9 PM, he went out and checked into Room 16 of the World Hotel at No. 9 Huage Nie Road, Eight Immortals Bridge. It is unknown what caused him to commit suicide by poisoning that night. At noon the next day, the tea server Zhang Asi (24 years old, from Shaoxing) tried to wake him up, but he did not respond after calling for a long time. He opened the door and went inside, finding Qiu already dead in bed. He immediately reported to the French police, who sent detectives to investigate. In the deceased's pocket, they found a note with his master's address. Zhang took the body to the S仁丰元 branch hall for examination. He also notified his master, as the deceased's family was still in the Ningbo countryside. His master sent a letter to notify them. The detective investigated the employer but could not ascertain the cause of the suicide. When Qiu went out on the evening of the 25th, he said he was going to a film company to shoot a movie. Yesterday morning, the French police reported the case to the Second Court, which appointed Prosecutor Wang Ren and a forensic scribe to the scene. They confirmed that the deceased had died from poisoning before death. The body has been handed over to the Tongren Funeral Home for temporary storage, awaiting family members to claim it. Later, the employer purchased clothes and a coffin for burial, and the coffin is temporarily stored in the hall, awaiting the arrival of family members from Shanghai to claim it.

Qian Chengxu Piloting a Light Industrial Shoe Factory 140

Qian Chengxu, secretary of the Chinese Industrial Federation, returned last year from an industrial inspection tour of Europe and the United States. Qian was very interested in light industry in Europe and America. After returning to China, he drafted various plans for establishing light industries, hoping to implement them. Recently, Qian started a pilot project for a light industrial cloth shoe factory. During the pilot period, he paid close attention to the robustness of the manufacturing, giving the shoes to coolies to wear in order to determine their durability. He will then make improvements and strive to reduce costs to meet the purchasing power of the general public. Once the trial is successful, he will officially establish a factory for production.

Resolution of Labor Dispute at the East China Tobacco Factory; Zhou Xuexiang and Others Appointed as Mediators 141

Dagon News reports that the East China Tobacco Factory on Tangshan Road in Hongkou employs over 1,000 male and female workers. In the past, the business was quite prosperous. However, due to the recent economic downturn and sluggish business, it had no choice but to issue a notice on the 28th of last month to lay off a large number of workers, which aroused the opposition of all the workers, who demanded that the decision be rescinded. This was not granted. The workers petitioned the party and government authorities to mediate. Due to the insistence of both parties, the matter has not yet been resolved. It is now known that Zhou Xuexiang, a standing committee member of the Shanghai General Labor Union, believes that the labor unrest has been delayed and unresolved, which is detrimental to social well-being. He specially invited Shen Changgeng and Zhang Shankun to serve as mediators. As a result, the factory paid each worker a severance payment, which the workers expressed satisfaction with, and the matter was declared to be resolved satisfactorily.

Death of Famous Doctor Yun Tieqiao 142

Yun Tieqiao, a renowned figure in the traditional Chinese medicine community, had been ill for a long time. Recently, he could not bear the intense heat, and his condition worsened. He passed away the night before last, at the age of fifty-eight. The traditional Chinese medicine community deeply mourns his passing. Decades ago, Yun was the editor of the Novel Monthly at the Commercial Press, and his literary reputation was well-known. Later, due to his weak health and frequent illnesses, he devoted himself to medicine and became famous as a doctor. He authored dozens of medical books that were widely circulated throughout the country. His theories combined Chinese and Western medicine, emphasizing practical experimentation and avoiding the old medical clichés. He was a pioneer in the recent trend of improving traditional Chinese medicine. During his lifetime, he ran the Tieqiao Medical Office, offering a correspondence consultation service with hundreds of remote disciples. He willed that his outstanding disciples Zhang Juying and his daughter, Ms. Huizhuang, continue to operate the office.

Gambling Case Cracked at the Oriental Hotel 143

The Old Gate Patrol Division of the Public Concession received a tip-off last night, claiming that people were gathering to gamble and skimming profits in Room 302 of the Oriental Hotel at the corner of Guangdong Road and Xizang Road. After receiving the information, the police secretly dispatched several Western detectives to apprehend the suspects at around 11 PM last night. They found gambling paraphernalia and smoking equipment in the room and arrested two individuals, including Ji. They were taken to the police station for temporary detention, awaiting transfer to the court for further investigation tomorrow morning. The hotel manager was also summoned for questioning.

Robbery at Renle Village, Luban Road 144

Yesterday morning, three robbers speaking with a Changshu accent suddenly came to the Qiu family residence at No. 23 Renle Village, Luban Road, in the French Concession. One was wearing a suit, one was wearing a white broadcloth short shirt and pants, and one was wearing a white shirt and shorts. Each was armed with a pistol and threatened the family members and servants to remain silent. They rummaged through boxes and cabinets for about twenty minutes, stealing eight pieces of men's and women's coarse and fine fur clothing, valued at over 500 yuan. They fled in a hurry with the stolen goods. When the local French police learned of the alarm, they immediately ordered Western and Chinese detectives to rush to the scene in police vehicles to pursue the robbers, but they had already disappeared without a trace. Later, the victim provided a detailed list of the losses to the police station, requesting them to investigate the stolen goods and robbers.

Impersonating a Detective and Defrauding; Five-Month Sentence 145

Li Bangyi (also known as Qi Qimei, Li Changgen, and Little Li), a native of Guangdong, recently impersonated a detective from the General Patrol Division and went to Xu Yongjia at the Yongming Printing Press at No. 422 Hede Road, falsely claiming that his worker Wu Hongbao had been arrested by the patrol division for robbing property from the Huasheng Printing Press in Hongkou. He offered to help for 500 yuan. Xu saw through his ploy and reported it to the General Patrol Division. Chinese detectives Jiang Shangpei and Gao Zhen arrested the imposter and handed him over to the First Special Court for interrogation and detention. The details have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhan Liangce opened the Second Criminal Court for continued hearing. Li was defended by lawyers Wu Peng. The police lawyer Zhang Shizhu stated that after the postponement, it was found that the defendant had used the same behavior in November of last year to defraud Chen Jimei, the owner of the Jimei Dancing School at No. 592 Sichuan Road, of 10 yuan. At that time, he told Chen Jimei that opening a dancing school required a donation for a license, otherwise it would have to be closed, causing Chen to be deceived. This case has also been filed. The court then questioned Li and allowed the lawyers for defense and the police to debate. Judge Zhan then announced the verdict, sentencing Li Bangyi to three months of imprisonment for each count of impersonating a public official and defrauding, to be served concurrently for a total of five months.

A Supplement to the Twenty-Five Histories Adds Unpublished Manuscripts of Wan Sitong 154

Following the Twenty-Five Histories, the Kaiming Bookstore is collecting tables and records from various series of books to publish a supplement to the Twenty-Five Histories. They have sought out various unpublished manuscripts and have obtained more than thirty types. Recently, they found fifteen unpublished manuscripts of Wan Sitong to add. Wan Sitong was a pioneer of Zhejiang East historical scholarship. His Historical Tables of Past Dynasties are well-known to almost every household. However, the Kangxi edition is incomplete. The full manuscript is stored in the Fufushi Studio of the Feng family in Yinxian County. Mr. Zhang Yongni of the same county will have it published in the Simingye Shu. Now, with the consent of Mr. Feng and Mr. Zhang, this manuscript will be published in the supplement to the Twenty-Five Histories first, and Mr. Zhang's collated notes will be attached to the end of the volume.

Weather Report 160

The Xujiahui Observatory's meteorological forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the Shandong area is cloudy and variable, with winds from the southeast to the southwest due to a low pressure system passing through Shanxi and moving eastward. The lower reaches of the Yangtze River are sunny and hot, gradually accumulating, with winds from the southeast to the east. The middle reaches of the Yangtze River have winds from the southeast to the southwest. The two hurricanes in the Pacific Ocean are gradually converging to form a single center point, moving northwestward. The East China Sea and Taiwan are cloudy, with strong northeasterly winds. The weather around the globe is bad. At 2 PM yesterday, the centers of the two hurricanes were within about 120 miles of 20 degrees north latitude and 128 degrees east longitude, moving northward, and within about 120 miles of 21 degrees north latitude and 132 degrees east longitude, moving northwestward. The wind force is unknown. Also, in the 24 hours before 3 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 96.1 degrees and the lowest was 87.1 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 98.6 degrees and the lowest was 78.3 degrees.

Chinese Team Had Good Technique but Lacked Experience, Resulting in a Loss with Dignity

Today, Chinese Team vs. Textile. The Chinese baseball team faced amateur teams from American and Japanese communities in China, marking the first game of the Shanghai Baseball League and the Chinese team's debut. Being newly formed, the Chinese team was no match for the seasoned amateur teams. However, their performance was still commendable. Unfortunately, due to a lack of prior match experience, they were flustered, and their formation was not strict, resulting in a 1-10 defeat. Today, the Chinese team will play against Shanghai Textile at 3 PM at the venue.

Balanced Situation. The Chinese team started on the offensive, with Jin Can hitting a single to first base. However, he was caught stealing at third base. His hitting technique is indeed clear, agile, and the forehand and backhand strokes are extremely proficient. The backhand is as powerful as the forehand. His backhand is unreliable, and he relies entirely on a single shot from the baseline. His skill level is comparable to that of Squier. His doubles play is more impressive, with excellent net play and smashing skills. If given proper training, he could be a formidable opponent with De Fu.

Lin vs. Squier. Squier is better than Lin in every aspect, and his tactics are very clever. His loss was not due to Lin's victory, but rather self-destruction. In the first set, Squier took the lead with 4-3, and Lin won two games. However, Squier won consecutive games to win the set. In the second set, Squier also won consecutive games, creating a sense of unstoppable momentum. Unexpectedly, due to too many mistakes, Lin won six games straight. In the third set, Squier took the lead with 3-1, but Lin again reversed the situation and won 6-4. Squier's hitting technique has greatly improved, but he still lacks stability. Otherwise, defeating Lin would have been easy.

Doubles Loss. The opponents in the Lin-Qiu doubles match did not seem particularly outstanding. However, Qiu Feihai's performance was lacking. His shots lacked control and went out of bounds repeatedly. His smashes were weak, and his teamwork was poor. Lin Baohua was unable to carry the team alone and was at a loss. In the first set, each team won their service games, and they even took the lead with 7-6. Unexpectedly, they lost three consecutive games. The second set was beyond salvage.

Hirai's Appearance. It was already late, and the audience began to leave. The match ended hastily. Sudo's performance was excellent, and Hirai was almost affected by it. The first set was 3-3, 5-5, and ended with 7-5. The second set was 2-2, 4-3, and ended with 6-4, reaching the height of tension.

Grand Occasion of the Guangdong Swimming Team's Open Competition 173

The He Sisters from Qingdao Join as Guest Performers

Two Little Heroes Also Participate in the Water

The Guangdong swimming team held an open swimming competition at the International Swimming Pool on Seymour Road at 8 PM the night before last (26th). More than 30 people registered to participate, and the He sisters, three female swimming prodigies who had just arrived in Shanghai from Qingdao, and a ten-year-old boy joined the performance. The audience was packed, and the event was a great success. The details are as follows:

Escape from a Sack and Somersaults. The first event was the 60-yard open freestyle, with more than 30 participants. They were divided into eight preliminary rounds, with the top two from each group advancing. The results of each group were acceptable, but they all made the mistake of not following the straight lane, which was due to a lack of practice. The escape from a sack was performed by the team's vice-captain, Zhong Choujun. He put himself in a large sack, weighed it down with several large stones, and tied the opening tightly. He escaped in just ten seconds, which earned him a lot of applause. The third act was somersaults, performed by Guo Ruiji of the Guangdong team, who performed six or seven somersaults in a row.

Three Sisters and Tall Men's Swimming. The fifth event was the tall men's swimming, performed by Huang Rixiong and Chen Baoyi of the Guangdong team, who connected each other and performed human movements. Next was the performance of the He sisters from Qingdao. First, Ms. Wu Wenjing performed the 60-yard freestyle, accompanied by Huang Rixiong of the Guangdong team. Next, Ms. He Wenjin performed the 60-yard breaststroke, accompanied by Wu Gansheng, the breaststroke king of the Guangdong team. Both ladies showed excellent posture and speed, especially Wenjin's breaststroke, which was exceptionally beautiful. Wenjin was the champagne of the previous Qingdao City.

Little Heroes and Diving Performances. Two little heroes showed their prowess in the water last night. Chen Youda, who was only twelve years old, bravely competed with many strong athletes. Although he did not win, it was not easy. The other, who was less than three feet tall, was said to be ten years old, but looked only seven or eight years old. He said his name was Lu Guolin. In addition to performing diving, he also performed the 60-yard breaststroke, without panicking, and with a natural attitude. The time at the finish line was one minute and nineteen seconds, which was remarkable. As for Chen Youda, who was eleven years old, in addition to participating in the 120-yard open backstroke, with a time of two minutes and twenty-seven and a half seconds, he also participated in the 210-yard breaststroke, but dropped out after four laps due to exhaustion. Next was the freestyle diving, performed by Deng Molin, Zhu Jiongpei, Chen Baoyi, and Huo Zhenghong of the Guangdong team.

Water Fight and Catching Ducks. In the water fight, Guangdong team captain and ice master Huang Rixiong was the champion. The method used was to float a large bamboo pole in the water. Two people crossed it, each striking with a firewood bag, and the one who fell into the water lost. Those who were knocked down by Huang included Dun Shoujun and Wu Gansheng, among others. In the end, Ouyang Wenliang knocked the champion into the water. Next was the duck catching performance, which was held in two groups. Guo Ruiji caught the duck in one minute in the first group, and Huo Zhenghong caught the duck in thirty-seven seconds in the second group. This act was particularly interesting, as the team members were eager to catch the duck, but the lively duck had already dived into the water, disappearing without a trace, earning applause from the ladies on both sides of the pool. The event ended at around 11 PM. The results of the open competition are attached below.

110-yard Freestyle Final: Lu Shungen, Guo Ruiji, 1 minute 41 seconds.

110-yard Breaststroke Final: Wang Weijun, Guo Ruiji, Chen Youda, 2 minutes 4 and 2/5 seconds.

Su Naichun, Jiang Wei, Jin Futian, 40 and 2/5 seconds.

Elementary School Principals and Teachers Exam Held in Beijing: Over 900 Applicants 174

Ministry of Education Announces Regulations for the National Compulsory Education Commission

The Ministry of Education announced on the 16th the organizational regulations of the National Compulsory Education Commission, consisting of ten articles. The original text is as follows: Article 1. In accordance with Article 27 of the Implementation Regulations of the Provisional Measures for the Implementation of Compulsory Education, the Ministry of Education shall organize the National Compulsory Education Commission (hereinafter referred to as the Commission) to assist in the implementation of compulsory education nationwide. Article 2. The main tasks of the Commission are as follows: A. To propose and review plans for the implementation of compulsory education. B. To review all regulations and measures concerning compulsory education. C. To assess the performance of each province and city in implementing compulsory education. Article 3. The members of the Commission are divided into the following categories: A. Ex officio members: 1. Minister of Education. 2. Vice Minister of Education. 3. One Counselor of the Ministry of Education. 4. Director and Section Chief of the First Section of the Department of General Education of the Ministry of Education. 5. Inspectors of the Ministry of Education. B. Appointed members: 5 to 7 people, appointed by the Minister of Education. Article 4. The Commission shall elect three Standing Committee members to handle daily affairs. Article 5. The plenary meeting of the Commission shall be held once every three months, with the Minister of Education as the chairman. Temporary meetings may be convened when necessary. The meeting period of the Standing Committee shall be determined by the Standing Committee members. Article 6. The Commission may convene representatives of the compulsory education commissions of each province and city to discuss matters related to the nationwide implementation of compulsory education when necessary. Article 7. The recommendations of the Commission regarding compulsory education shall be implemented after approval by the Ministry of Education. Article 8. The Commission may appoint staff members, who shall be concurrently filled by members of the Ministry of Education. Article 9. All members of the Commission shall hold nominal positions. Appointed members who attend meetings and handle affairs may receive appropriate travel expenses. Article 10. These regulations shall be promulgated and implemented by the Ministry of Education.

A Feat of Summer Long-Distance Walking: Scout Xu Tai Sets Off from Shanghai Yesterday 180

Expected to Reach Destination in Over 40 Days of Hiking Through Jiangsu, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Hubei

Along the Way, He Will Investigate Local Customs and Scout Activities

Xu Tai (zi Guping), the leader of the second team of the 818th regiment of the Chinese Boy Scouts, has served in the Scouting world for many years and is accustomed to hiking. This time, Mr. Xu decided to use the summer vacation to embark on a solo summer long-distance hiking trip through the four provinces of Jiangsu, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Hubei, to investigate local customs and Scout activities. All preparations have been completed, and he set off from the North Station at 2 PM yesterday, hiking along the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway through Suzhou, Zhenjiang, and Nanjing. Then, from Nanjing, he will go upstream along the Yangtze River into Anhui, passing through Caishi, Dangtu, Wuhu, Tongling, Datong, Guichi, and Dongliu, then passing through Xiaogushan to Hukou, crossing the river to Jiujiang, climbing Guling Lushan, taking a short rest, and then passing through Wuchang to the destination of Hankou. The journey is expected to take over 40 days. He will stay in major ports for one day and in other places for one or two hours. The Shanghai Scout Council and the regiment leader, Zhi Bingshou, have already telegraphed the local authorities to take care of and protect Mr. Xu when he passes through, and to provide him with convenience. Party and government figures, such as Yu Youren, Duan Qirui, Wu Tiecheng, Du Yuesheng, Wang Xiaolai, Wang Zhen, Xu Peihuang, and Tonghang Bai, all believe that Mr. Xu's ambition is commendable and have written inscriptions to encourage him, adding to Mr. Xu's grand departure. When he set off yesterday, many people from all walks of life went to the station to see him off.

Major Financial Players Vigorously Purchase, Standard Gold Price Soars Alarmingly 182

Once Approached the 880 Yuan Mark, Rose Another 5.4 Yuan, Still Above the Closing Price

Yesterday, the overseas silver price was inconsistent. The market opened slightly weak. Unexpectedly, the Central Bank's listed price suddenly increased, sparking a buying frenzy. The price broke through the 70 yuan mark. Major players' appetite for buying increased, and the upward trend became difficult to contain. The exchange rate followed closely, once approaching the 80 yuan mark. The Hong Kong market was normal, and sellers took advantage of the high price to operate. One bank vigorously sold off, and the Hong Kong market turned cheaper. The Indian silver price was expected to rise, and the decline was also rapid. However, it ultimately remained above the closing price. It was observed that the overseas silver market did not fall much in the morning, and there was still a rebound after the closing. The forward silver price in Mont Dele slightly fell by 0.5 to 2.5%. The exchange rate slightly increased, and the London spot gold price fell by 2.5 pence. A dispatch from the Associated Press stated that President Roosevelt sent a letter to silver-supporting senators, expressing his continued support for the silver policy. The market opened weakly, and off-exchange trading opened at 66-67 yuan, then fell to 5 yuan. The Central Bank's listed price was announced, with both British and American currencies shrinking, and the customs gold unit rose by 9%. The standard gold price rose to 872.2 yuan, and sentiment recovered. After opening, the price immediately broke through the 70 yuan mark. Despite some fluctuations, the internal market followed closely. HSBC's listed price for British currency shrunk by 0.25, and American currency shrunk by 0.5 yuan. The buying sentiment in the market was extremely strong, and major players such as Chunyuan, Yongyuan, Shengyong, and others continued to buy. The price rose sharply, once approaching the 80 yuan mark. The Hong Kong market was normal, and buyers operated and slightly turned flat, but there were still many rebounds. Later, the Hong Kong market turned cheaper by 1.125, and sentiment slightly weakened. Major players sold off more actively. There were rumors that certain banks came out to sell, coupled with Reuters' report that Indian silver was expected to rise by 6 annas, and the price retreated into the 70 yuan mark twice. Ultimately, with buyers still pouring in, the market situation continued to be firm at noon. The overall trend in the first half of the day was volatile, and both short sellers and long sellers closed out positions, causing considerable confusion in the middle. Spring and Autumn Children's Weekly

Please mobilize all children! (Lecture Hall) 192

— Jun Peng

Children! Now is the time to use your strength! Everyone quickly issue a general mobilization order! Children who read the newspaper should know that Shanghai has compulsory literacy education, which has started on July 1st. Although there are more than 60,000 illiterate people who have enthusiastically enrolled, do you think this counts as popularizing education when more than 80 percent of China is illiterate?

Literacy is a tool for seeking knowledge, and knowledge is the driving force for developing all undertakings. The strength of a country depends on the level of knowledge of its people. To seek a high level of knowledge, we must popularize education. Now, to save our precarious motherland, this is the only way. Therefore, I ask all children to use their sincere hearts to teach illiterate people to read.

Children! Don't think that we are young and don't have much ability, but you must know that we are powerful warriors in this movement! It doesn't take much effort for us to teach people to read. Just teach the words that the teacher teaches you every day to illiterate people, one by one. In this way, one teaches ten, ten teaches a hundred, and we guide each other in turn. It is not difficult to achieve the goal of compulsory literacy education.

Children all over the country, during this hot summer vacation, you probably don't have much summer homework. You can always take some time to implement the "little teacher" system, take on this extremely important mission, and serve the country and the nation. At that time, how glorious and respectable the "little teacher" will be!

Etiquette at a Banquet (Civic Training) 193

— Kang Jian Zhai Fu

If we participate in a tea party or a dinner party, we must pay attention to the etiquette of eating and drinking.

When entering the seat, be sure to identify your appropriate seat. After entering the seat, every word and action should always take care of those at the same table, and don't be a strange person doing things separately. Also, don't show a rude and reckless appearance to annoy people.

When chewing things, don't open your mouth too wide. Don't chew from side to side like cattle and sheep eating grass. Don't have your mouth full of food. Chew slowly and deliberately. Be especially careful that things don't get stuck in your nasal cavity or trachea, coughing and sneezing are the most impolite.

When drinking tea and swallowing rice, it is best to do so lightly and without making a sound. Don't make gulping sounds like cattle and sheep drinking water, or donkeys and horses chewing grass.

At the banquet, do not spread your elbows and encroach on the seat of your neighbors. Every move must be gentle and elegant.

When pouring wine, you must stand up. Don't drink too much. Wine should be drunk slowly. Don't force people to drink too much.

As a guest, every meal and drink should leave some surplus. The host should let the guests finish their meal and then stop eating, so as not to make the guests feel uneasy.

Uproar in Heaven 194

— Wei Bingxin

Bright flashes, loud rumblings, thunder and lightning open the stage for the uproar in heaven.

Dense clouds, like a smoke screen, the color is thick;

Wild wind, like a tiger roaring, the sound is loud;

Heavy rain, like a sea pouring, the momentum is surging.

It's like an aerial battle, thousands of troops and horses are charging together.

In an instant, the clouds move, and the sun raises its head and shows its smile.

The wind has blown, the rain has stopped, and the thunder has no sound and the lightning has no trace.

It's like the aerial battle has closed, the flags have been lowered and the drums have been silenced, and the attack has stopped.

Why is the Indoor Temperature Different? (Common Sense) 195

— Chu Yu

Recently, the weather is getting hotter every day. Every family has built awnings and covered curtains to prevent direct sunlight. However, the indoor temperature varies from household to household due to the size of the house, the presence or absence of surrounding trees, and the type of windows. Moreover, the summer heat in the city is more severe than in the countryside. However, the color of the tiles on the roof and the paving materials of the road have the greatest impact on the summer heat. Why? When the sun's heat shines on the roof of a house, according to scientists' experiments, a roof covered with red tiles absorbs 67%, a roof covered with green bricks absorbs 75%, and a black galvanized iron roof absorbs 77%. This is because the materials used for the roof are different and the color difference causes the heat absorption to be high or low. Other factors such as the surrounding roads and patios of the house also affect the temperature. Although the temperature of the road varies depending on the location and time, roughly speaking, for an air temperature of 28.8 degrees, the heat absorbed is as follows: wood-brick road is 45.0 degrees, asphalt road is 42.3 degrees, yellow sand cement mixed road is 39.0 degrees, stone road is 38.4 degrees, and yellow sand road is 36.0 degrees. Judging from this, the paved road is actually hotter. Therefore, in today's world with developed transportation, paving is necessary due to the demands of the public. On the one hand, to reduce the summer heat and facilitate pedestrians, planting trees along the road is both spectacular and can avoid the heat.

The Cricket is Chirping 196

— Chonglou

When the cicada's song in the tree has not yet stopped, the cricket in front of the steps has already chirped.

We all know that the cicada is a leisurely and comfortable animal; in the summer, it does not do any work, it only knows how to sing loudly: when the weather gradually gets cold, it will starve to death because it has not prepared food, but the cricket is different from the cicada. The cricket's chirp is very meaningful. It is reporting to us that autumn has already arrived, and we should not be taking in the cool air, but we should hurry up and work hard on our own careers; and the cricket is brave. When others bully it, it will definitely resist bravely and never shrink back.

Dear little friends! When you hear the cricket chirping, do you also think that the year is coming to an end and you should make a final effort? And when you see the cricket's brave spirit, are you also prepared to overcome your inner fears, to forge your strong physique, and to be a healthy little citizen?

Talking to Children About Their Own Newspaper (Conversation) 198

— Ji Yu

What is the function of a newspaper? Newspapers roughly have two functions: one is to guide the people, so that the people can obtain various kinds of knowledge. For example, if children read the newspaper every day, their knowledge will progress in all directions. The other is to convey the opinions of the people, so the newspaper is also called the "mouthpiece of the people", and journalists are called "uncrowned emperors".

Where does news come from? There are two sources of news: the first is collected by the newspaper's own reporters or correspondents, and the second is obtained from news agencies. There are two types of news agencies: government-run and commercial. The purpose of government-run agencies is to publicize themselves, and the purpose of commercial agencies is to make money. There are many foreign news agencies in our country, such as Reuters, Associated Press, and Havas, etc., which can often be seen in newspapers. Our own news agencies also exist, such as the Central News Agency, National News Agency, Guowen News Agency, Shenshi News Agency, and Xinsheng News Agency, all of which are national news agencies, numbering about 160.

What is the history of our own newspaper? The oldest newspaper in China today is the Shen Bao, which you are reading, which has been published for more than 60 years. The second oldest is the Xinwen Bao, which has also been published for more than 40 years. Since the publication of the Shen Bao, our own Chinese newspapers have gradually increased. Now, there are more than 400 registered newspapers in the country.

The Science Teacher Does Magic (Science Game) 199

— He Gongchao

The Strange Glass

The science teacher came on stage with a glass and a piece of paper. He said to the children below the stage: "Today, my magic trick is simple, but also interesting."

He put the piece of paper on the edge of the table, poured half a glass of water into the cup, and pressed the cup on the piece of paper, saying:

"Children, who can take the piece of paper in your hand without moving the glass?"

The children below the stage all thought: "The piece of paper is pressed under the glass. If you want to take the piece of paper out without moving the glass, it is impossible!" Therefore, not a single child stood up and said: "I can, I can."

The science teacher smiled and said: "Actually, this is the easiest thing to do. Watch." He quickly and forcefully pulled the piece of paper, and the glass did not move at all, but the piece of paper was already in his hand. Then, the children below the stage all opened their surprised eyes and praised the simplicity and fun of the science teacher's magic trick in their hearts.

The science teacher said: "Do you know why the cup didn't move? Originally, all stationary objects cannot move by themselves. The copper coins on the table will never fly into your hands by themselves. At the same time, all moving objects cannot stop by themselves. The wood rolling down from the top of the mountain will never stop halfway. This property of objects is called "inertia". But if we use our hands to take the copper coins, the copper coins will move; if we take big stones to block the wood, the wood will stop; breaking this inertia is called "force". Just now, I used my hand to hit the piece of paper, and the "force" only reached the piece of paper, and did not reach the cup. The cup's inertia was not broken, so it still didn't move.

"However, when you try it, if you pull it slowly, the cup will follow the piece of paper. This is what you should pay attention to."

Children's Haha Troupe (Entertainment News) 200

— Ouyang Gu

Recently, the Hangzhou People's Club, in order to promote children's health and promote entertainment, has specially organized a "Children's Haha Troupe". Anyone aged between eight and fifteen can participate freely. The main purpose of the troupe is: to require three big laughs every day, to hold a troupe meeting every week, and to hold a haha meeting once within the prescribed period, to perform various interesting skills to increase interest. It is said that after the announcement of this news, dozens of students from private primary schools such as XX have already registered to join the People's Club.

Children! What do you think after hearing the above news? I must tell you that laughter, from a physiological point of view: on the one hand, it can eliminate troubles, and on the other hand, it can liven up the body and mind. It is indeed a good way to prolong life. At the same time, we can't feel tired when we do anything. In addition, it can make a thing progress smoothly without fear of difficulties. Therefore, we must imitate the "Children's Haha Troupe" organized by the Hangzhou People's Club, or if there are brothers and sisters at home, gathering together can also organize a similar haha troupe, stipulating three big laughs every day. Isn't this also very interesting?

Children! Don't be silent anymore, now is the time for children to cheer up! Get up and do something that is beneficial to your body and mind!

The Mouse Was Originally a Mouse (Indian Fairy Tale) 202

— Yue Qi

In ancient times, a hermit found a little mouse; it had escaped from the claws of an eagle. He pitied it and used magic to turn it into a young girl, whom he brought home to raise. When she grew up, he hoped to marry her to someone powerful. He summoned the sun and said to him, "Take this girl as your wife, I want to marry her to someone powerful." The sun replied, "The clouds are more powerful than me, they can cover me." The hermit heard what the sun said, and ordered him to go back, summoned the clouds, and made the same proposal to him. The clouds replied, "The wind is more powerful than me; it can blow me away." The hermit summoned the wind and made the same proposal to him. The wind replied, "The mountains are more powerful than me, because I cannot move them." So the hermit summoned the Himalayas and made the same proposal to him. The mountain replied, "Mice are more powerful than me, because they can dig holes in me."

So the hermit summoned a mountain mouse and said to him, "Take this girl as your wife." The mouse replied, "I am willing, but how can she walk into my cave!" His words were reasonable, so the hermit said, "Then turn her back into a mouse." He used magic to turn her back into a mouse and told the male mouse to take her away.

Waste Utilization 203

— (Ning Ziqiang)

Rags can be used to make paper, which is of considerable value in terms of waste utilization. Now, I will teach you how to utilize a piece of waste. The effectiveness of the result is truly incredible. You can achieve it in one go, so why not do it?

Use an old Mobiloil lampshade. Only the bottom needs to be complete, and the top can be broken. Then, make a funnel shape out of paper and place it on top of the lampshade. Add a little sugar water. Place the lampshade on your desk. Soon, flies will come to patronize it. The flies will perch on the funnel, sucking the sugar water, and become so happy that they forget to return. In that case, this tiny fly will fall to its death.

Children's Corner

### My Summer Vacation 204

— Cao Honghui

Time flies so fast. It hasn't been many days since the spring semester started, and now it's summer vacation again. However, in this semester, because I didn't study hard on weekdays, my grades were not good. When the vacation started, the homeroom teacher said that I was barely promoted to the next grade. When I heard the teacher's words, I felt very ashamed, and I thought to myself that I had failed the teacher's earnest teachings. When I returned home, my older sister told my parents what the teacher had said, and my parents scolded me for not studying hard. After being scolded, I stopped being naughty, even though it was summer vacation.

My parents scolded me because they wanted me to improve. I thought that in the next semester, when I entered the lower class of the second grade, the knowledge would definitely be much better than that of the upper class. Therefore, during this summer vacation, in addition to doing the "vacation homework" from school, I will also seriously review the lessons I usually missed from the beginning. I will get up early every morning to practice writing, and when I have free time, I will read the various children's books and newspapers that my father bought. If there are any characters I don't know, I will ask my father or look them up in the dictionary myself. I think this way, I can make up for my shortcomings.

Now, I am writing about my past mistakes and my summer vacation and submitting it to the Children's Weekly. I also hope that other children like me will also "correct their mistakes" like me. Let's all work hard and do self-study. If we keep doing this, we will not be held back in the future.

Children's Fiction

### The Little Drummer (1) 205

— Xin Qing

July 24, 1848, was the first day of the Battle of Custoza. In one of our infantry battalions, sixty soldiers were ordered to defend a house on a nearby plateau. But they were suddenly attacked by two teams of Austrian soldiers. Because they were attacked from all sides, they did not have time to hide in the house and block the door, so they had to leave their dead and wounded comrades and lie in the fields.

The door was finally defended and blocked very firmly. Our soldiers hurried to the windows on the ground floor and the upper floor to desperately fire back at the attacking enemies, while the enemies were slowly advancing in a semicircle, fiercely counterattacking.

The sixty Italian soldiers were commanded by two lieutenants, and their commander was a silent and solemn old colonel, who was tall and had snow-white temples.

With them was a Sardinian little drummer, a child about fourteen years old, who looked like twelve because of his short stature. His skin was olive-colored, and in his deep-set black eyes, there seemed to be flames burning.

The old colonel commanded the soldiers to resist from upstairs. Every time he issued an order, it was as fast as firing a pistol. His iron-blue face was calm and expressionless.

The little drummer, pale-faced, stood on the table, his hands holding onto the wall, leaning out the window, and saw the Austrian soldiers passing through the fields in the haze of smoke.

The house was located on top of a sloping hillside, with a high, small window upstairs that could overlook the top of the hill. There were no Austrian soldiers in sight on this side of the hill. Their guns and cannons were attacking the front and sides of the house. This attack could not have been more violent. The shells hit the walls like lightning, passed through the broken roof, destroyed the ceiling, shattered the beams and pillars, doors and windows, and all the equipment. The air was filled with bricks, wood chips, and plaster like clouds. The sound of shattering glass and objects rang out overhead, echoing the terrible sound of guns and cannons.

The soldiers who resisted at the windows fell down from time to time after being shot, and someone would immediately drag them aside. Other soldiers ran back and forth in the rooms, covering the bleeding wounds on their bodies with their hands. In the kitchen lay a soldier, a bullet had pierced his forehead. The enemies were constantly surrounding them. The silent and solemn old colonel finally showed an uneasy appearance, rushed out of the room, and a sergeant followed him. After a while, the sergeant rushed back again and called the little drummer to go with him.
