Women's Corner

### Further Discussion on Law and Women, and a Response to the Sunday Review of the Ta Wan Pao 206

— Jennie

In this month's twenty-first issue of the Ta Wan Pao Sunday Review, there is a short commentary titled "Don't Marry a Man Who Has a Wife," which is a criticism of the writer's "Law and Women" article in the last issue of this publication. Although it is a humble and insightful opinion, the writer dares not agree. Therefore, I would like to further express my humble opinion as follows: (The original text of the Ta Wan Pao short commentary is appended to the right for readers to refer to.)

First, I remember that in my previous article, I clearly said, "In a feudal patriarchal society, a powerful young master could have three wives and four concubines, and society would praise and promote it, and the law would guarantee it in many ways. Although the present era has changed..." But our critic has taken the words out of context, lightly crossed out the sentence "In a feudal patriarchal society," and deprived my words of their temporality. Everyone knows that in the past feudal society, it was considered a blessing and a good thing for a young master to have three wives and four concubines. All kinds of legends and novels, such as the Nine Beauties Picture and the Ten Beauties Picture, depict a romantic talent surrounded by women, like a butterfly flitting among flowers. Isn't this "praised and promoted by society"? Moreover, in many places, it was considered indecent for a wealthy man's family not to have a few concubines. Therefore, it is not "overstated" to say that "society praises and promotes it." As for the law, before the implementation of laws and regulations in our country, all historical records and classics clearly wrote about men having multiple wives: "The Book of Rites" has the sentence: "When buying a concubine, if you don't know her surname, then divine it." The Gongyang Commentary records: "A prince marries nine women, and the emperor marries twelve women." During the Qin Dynasty, there were even titles such as "Lady in the Palace, Beauty, Fair Person, Eight Sons, Seven Sons, Elder Attendant, Younger Attendant," etc. During the reign of Emperor Wu of the Han Dynasty, even more titles were added, such as Jieyu and Zhaoyi, totaling fourteen grades. Zhong Changtong said: "In the palaces of dukes and marquises, there are hundreds of beauties, and in the homes of rural scholars, there are dozens of concubines." These are all true and reliable facts, and we don't need to cover up for the ancients. As for the implementation of laws and regulations, such as the law of inheritance and the provisions of "recognizing concubines as members of the family," the law clearly protected polygamy. Therefore, it is not "overstated" to say that "the law protects it in many ways"!

Since the abolition of the law of inheritance in the twentieth year of the Republic of China, up to the recent promulgation of the new criminal law, the relationship between the law of our country and women has indeed been considerably improved. However, in the current society, can the so-called "social perception" represent the perception of the general society?

Second, Article 239 of the new criminal law is indeed a crime that can only be prosecuted upon complaint. If the spouse condones or forgives the adultery, they may not file a complaint. If the young master has a new love, and the original spouse does not file a complaint, then the young master is still innocent. In other words, there is this law, but women will not use it, do not use it, or do not want to use it. This is not that the law is ineffective, but that women are voluntarily giving up. However, according to general common sense, unless she is an idiot, disabled, or insane, she will never condone her spouse committing adultery or even marrying someone else. From the standpoint of freedom of marriage, if one party has a new love, the other party does not need to be overly attached. Moreover, sexual love is always exclusive. Knowing that the husband has a new love but still being attached—euphemistically called condoning or forgiving, and being a "nominal couple"—there must be unavoidable difficulties! When most women still regard marriage as a lifelong nursing home, if the husband is imprisoned, it is tantamount to blocking or breaking their own rice bowl. Therefore, it is better to endure humiliation for the future than to seek temporary pleasure and vent anger. At the same time, even if they can file a complaint, if the other party (husband) is a person of power, the law will be helpless! As long as they don't "cover their ears," they won't be "unaware" of such facts!

Third, admittedly, there are many women who are eager to curry favor with the powerful or marry wealthy old men, willing to make "worthless sacrifices for vanity." However, in the current society, which is clad in a capitalist veneer but still retains feudal remnants internally and has a dilapidated economic structure, most women cannot make a living independently and naturally have to rely on men. The temptation of a luxurious society makes them tend towards vanity, which is a common problem in capitalist societies. Therefore, vanity has its economic roots and cannot be cured by women's self-improvement and self-encouragement. Moreover, when most women are simply commodities that can be bought and sold at will, and the powerful use their omnipotent money and mountain-like influence to buy a weak woman like a commodity, it takes no effort at all. Who dares to believe that "such things can be eradicated"?

Of course, we believe that "such things will eventually be eradicated." But this can only be realized when people are truly equal and free.

Only then will the law be a law that protects the interests of the general public. Therefore, we do not despise the law, but we should see through the current law, especially the relationship between the current law and women. The sociologist Bebel said: "The law of a country is the expression of the advantageous organization of the ruling class. Women are the oppressed and submissive 'sex,' so their position in the law is also the same. The law is passive and active. When distributing rights, it pays no attention to the oppressed; this is passive. When pointing out the submissive position of the oppressed and specifying various exceptions for its own convenience, it is active." (See Women and Society, p. 431). These words clearly tell us the relationship between law in an unequal society and the powerful and the oppressed, especially the relationship with women.

In short, to think that all current laws and social perceptions will never change due to power, and that inequality between men and women can be achieved as long as women strive for self-improvement and self-encouragement, is either ignorance of the social reality or an intentional distortion of the facts.

### Don't Marry a Man Who Has a Wife 207

Today's Shen Bao "Women's Corner" weekly published a commentary entitled "Law and Women," written by Jennie.

There are two points in this article that raise my doubts. First, the author said: "A powerful young master can have three wives and four concubines, and society praises and promotes it. The law protects it in many ways." These words are somewhat exaggerated and unrealistic. Not only does our country's law not explicitly protect polygamy, but it is also often criticized by society under the current circumstances. It is not because of the relationship of the young master that the social perception and legal provisions can be changed. Second, Article 239 of the new criminal law stipulates: "Whoever has a spouse and commits adultery with another person shall be sentenced to imprisonment for up to one year..." This is a crime that can only be prosecuted upon complaint, and if the spouse condones or forgives it, they may not file a complaint. Therefore, it is believed that this new law has failed if the young master has a new love and the original spouse does not file a complaint. We dare not say so.

In short, what we hope for from the women's world is that women themselves will strive for self-improvement and self-encouragement, and hold the principle of "not marrying a man who has a wife." Then such things can be eradicated. Otherwise, because of temporary vanity, not only is the sacrifice worthless, but it also exposes the weakness of women.

——Recorded from the Ta Wan Pao Sunday Review of the twenty-first of this month

Women's Issues Seminar

### Section 5: Prostitution and Trafficking in Women 208

— Jun Hui

Prostitution is not a phenomenon unique to capitalist society. Large-scale prostitution systems also existed in the era of slave economies and feudalism. However, in the era of capitalism, it has gained a more widespread social foundation.

Capitalism turns women's bodies into a major commodity on the market, making them subject to the laws of commodity circulation like bacon, rubber, and cotton. On the one hand, people who cannot get marital satisfaction under the "sacred" monogamy system and the vast number of forced celibates—such as soldiers, students, and workers—need to satisfy momentary pleasure without any responsibility for women's bodies. At the same time, on the other hand, fallen aristocratic women, bankrupt peasant women, and unemployed female workers are forced by hunger and cold to sell their bodies. They are concentrated in capitalist prostitution enterprises through various agents. Thus, the process of supply and demand circulation is accurately implemented. In this way, the "human flesh market" of capitalist society is formed.

In capitalist society, because the profits of prostitution enterprises are particularly large, merchants who only care about profit sell women and run prostitution businesses in various ways. On the one hand, they buy young and beautiful "cash cows," and on the other hand, they attract customers who are willing to pay. In public brothels, tea houses, theaters, dance halls, and other places, human flesh trading is openly or secretly practiced. There are high-ranking officials, judges, politicians, gentlemen, and soldiers, and even the core figures of the anti-prostitution movement become their customers.

Regarding the capitalist enterprise form of prostitution, Professor Plekhanov, the author of "European Prostitution," provides very interesting information. He first pointed out the trade routes of livelihood commodities: "Most prostitutes are exported from Hungary, Galicia, Poland, and Romania, and transported to Brazil, Argentina, South America, and Asia Minor." He also said: "In Budapest, it takes 500,000 kronen to open the latest brothel. In Paris, the annual income of a second-rate prostitution enterprise reaches 70,000 francs. A newly operated brothel in Berlin has a capital of one million marks, and it is said that it distributed a 20% dividend in 1912."

Thus, in capitalist society, prostitution is a "low-risk, high-return" enterprise, and this enterprise also provides considerable assistance to national finance. The memory of the so-called "menstrual tide" of prostitutes in Foshan, Guangdong, a few months ago who wanted to be exempted from paying flower taxes is still fresh in our minds. This so-called "flower tax" is the same in all countries, and it is something that is exploited from prostitutes to enrich the national treasury. Therefore, the state has the responsibility to protect the prostitution industry that pays taxes. On the other hand, because the "human flesh market" is too exposed to the ugliness of this civilized society, they often use a moral "veil" to cover it up. They either issue government orders to prohibit prostitution, or launch mass anti-prostitution movements to abolish it. But this is like Don Quixote fighting windmills, and it eventually fails. The more they want to cover it up, the more the ugliness is exposed.

Originally, the commodification of women's bodies and the commodification of human labor belong to the same category. In a society where the "labor market" exists, the so-called "human flesh market" will inevitably follow. If it is wrong for women to sell their bodies, then it is also wrong for workers to sell their blood and sweat! However, in the eyes of the ruling class, the public circulation of these living commodities is not only "unsightly" but also "damages public morals," so they come up with various methods of suppression to decorate the moral facade of society.

But when they cannot cover up this ugly social phase, they retreat and look for a theoretical basis to rationalize the prostitution system. But this basis is also found in women! Dr. Lobano, a famous German hygiene scholar, explained the inevitability and perpetuity of the prostitution system as follows:

"Women's prostitution exists in any nation and any era, and it cannot be abolished. Because this system is effective for sexual intercourse and originates from human nature. The motivation for prostitution is mostly due to the innate weakness of women. Just as there are genius idiots, giant dwarfs, and ordinary mediocre people in a nation, due to the pranks of creation, there are abnormal people who must prostitute themselves." (Women and Society)

This is obviously an attempt to place the responsibility for the ugly behavior of society on women and make the profitable prostitution enterprise a rational existence. At the same time, this is the consistent view of all those who defend this society.

In our opinion, the phenomenon of prostitution did not exist when women first appeared in this world. Although the Bible says that Eve is the devil who tempts men, in the primitive matriarchal society of communal production and consumption, women did not have "innate weaknesses," and there was no prostitution system. It was only in the patriarchal era when most people engaged in production and a few people specialized in consumption that prostitution was discovered. But we are absolutely unwilling to push the responsibility for this social evil onto men, but should push it onto the unreasonable social system.

In short, the prostitution system is something that is bound to arise in a society dominated by the propertied and male power. Therefore, launching a so-called anti-prostitution movement in a society of propertied people and attempting to eliminate it is only a delusional dream. We believe that prostitution is not based on human sacrifice and the weakness of women, nor is it something that "coexists with heaven and earth." When it comes to a society where no one is allowed to eat without working, just like the primitive matriarchal era where everyone produces and everyone consumes, the prostitution system will also be eliminated along with all other unreasonable systems, which can be asserted!

Novella

### Returning Home 209

— Su Hong

——Her? She wants to take everything from me. This thing, "Mom! Give it to me." That thing, "Mom! Give it to me." I tell you, she even wants to take my spinning wheel." Pointing to a spinning wheel in front of the door, she continued, "Indeed, she was born into a hard life. Your brother-in-law used to work for others, but he got jaundice last year and hasn't recovered yet. The whole family relies on your sister to scratch and crawl for a living. Fortunately, her eldest daughter is grown up. She's thirteen this year. She said that after the younger siblings go to sleep at night, she can have the eldest daughter spin yarn for others and earn some money."

Xiuzhen shrank her body further into the quilt.

Mother began to take off her clothes and sat in the quilt, feeling for lice in her collar.

Suddenly, the sister-in-law next door started hitting the child, the floor thumped, and she cursed:

——You little devil, you spilled water again. Do you know that in this cold weather, if the quilt gets wet, how are we going to sleep?"

——Grandma! Grandma! I'm dying of pain!" the child screamed sharply.

——Stop hitting him, he's already spilled it, what's the use of hitting him?" Mother said loudly.

——Don't interrupt, if I don't hit him, he'll spill it again next time. Will you spill it next time? Tell me!" The sister-in-law said hatefully. Then there was the sound of whipping again.

——Say it, say it! "I won't spill it next time," say it and I won't hit you." Mother taught her eldest grandson.

After a round of beatings and scoldings, it seemed that the child had admitted his mistake. For a moment, it was quiet again.

The light was very small, the oil was almost burned out. Usually, if Mother wasn't doing anything, she would blow out the light when she went to sleep. Now, for her daughter's sake, she got up again, poked the wick up a bit, and added some oil.

——Oil is really expensive." Mother said, "In the past, a hundred coins could last for many days, but now it burns out in a few days. The more I save, the faster it runs out. Sometimes I even go to bed in the dark!" She put down the curtain, startling the rats, which scurried around on top of the curtain. The cat lying at the foot of the bed was startled and jumped up. The rats squeaked.

——Why are you still keeping a cat?" Xiuzhen asked.

——How can I not keep one? The rats are so hateful, they bite everything to pieces." Mother suddenly smiled. "My cat is very well-behaved. Every day it always drags a few rats, and I don't need to feed it." Speaking of food, she thought of rice. "Rice is still so expensive! Two dimes can't even buy a liter of rice. … Sigh, we are suffering too much. Your brother can't find a job, and he hasn't even sent a letter back. I don't even know where he is."

——How is sister-in-law coping?" Xiuzhen asked.

——You'll know slowly. It's time to sleep."

Mother took off her cotton clothes and slowly lay down in the quilt, closing her mouth tightly as if she had fallen asleep comfortably.

But Xiuzhen still had her eyes open, and it seemed like there was a worm crawling in her brain. She clearly heard the watchman strike the third watch.

(3)

Mother sat on the porch basking in the sun, her small feet resting on a "tiger head" (a basket made of yellow mud, which can hold charcoal fire. Poor people in the countryside mostly use this to keep warm). Her mouth kept chanting Buddhist scriptures. Xiuzhen sat next to her mother, her hands folded, like a monkey.

The sister-in-law ran out, carrying a one-year-old child in one arm and a five- or six-year-old boy in the other, with a large bundle of diapers under her arm, dragging her feet. She put the child next to Mother and hung the diapers one by one on the bamboo pole.

Another child suddenly shouted inside: "Mom! I want to get up! Mom!..."

The sister-in-law moved the bamboo pole to a place where the sun was shining, and scolded anxiously:

——You little devil, I was just about to dress you and get you up, but you said no. Now I'm busy doing things, but you want to get up. You little devil, where do I have the time! I haven't even borrowed rice for lunch yet! You little devil, you keep shouting, even if we're not poor, you'll shout us into poverty."

Mother put down her rosary and hurried in, saying repeatedly, "Baby! Grandma will dress you, don't cry, come with Grandma to bask in the sun."

Young Mistress Wang and her maid also carried out a small table, preparing to make silver ingots in the sun. The sister-in-law changed her face and said a few polite words:

——Young Mistress Wang! You're really good at it, making silver ingots in this cold weather."

——If I don't do it, it'll be too late. Tomorrow is already the end of the month. Once it's past the twentieth, I won't have time to do it. It's a little busier these days..."

——Oh! Young Mistress Wang!" The sister-in-law leaned her head into Young Mistress Wang's ear and said in a low voice, "Lend me two liters of rice."

——I don't have any extra rice. I only exchanged half of this year's rent rice. Of course, I won't have enough to eat myself next year." (To be continued)

Amateur Essays

On the Education of Talents 212

— Yi Ren

Some say that the disease of education in China today lies in the lack of its popularization. Therefore, the people's wisdom cannot be improved, the training of citizens cannot be implemented, production technology cannot be improved, the people's livelihood and economy cannot be developed, and the national concept and global vision cannot be established. Therefore, the advocacy of universal education or compulsory education is indeed the goal of future education, which is almost self-evident and leaves no room for rebuttal. However, observing the trends of modern world politics, the strength of a country is not only due to the improvement of the general people's knowledge, but also relies on the grand plans and strategies of outstanding leaders. That is to say, the use of "power" and "ability" must go hand in hand without conflict, so that they complement each other, and only then can the country have hope of being well-governed.

Based on this argument, we can know that popular education is to improve the general people's wisdom, and we must devote all our efforts to promote its success; and in addition to popular education, we must also focus on the education of talents at the same time. The education of talents is to cultivate the nation's capable people. The country must have good politicians to handle political affairs, scientists to create inventions, and educators, writers, and entrepreneurs, etc., each standing at the forefront of society, in order to lead the people of the whole country onto the road to prosperity. Therefore, it is said that the talent education movement and the popular education movement should be given equal importance and should not be biased.

Are the young people who are currently receiving university education or the prospective doctors who are gilded abroad the capable people of the country we are talking about? I think probably no one would dare to make a judgment! To be honest, more than 99% of those who receive higher education today are children of the bourgeoisie. Although there are no shortage of good young people who are dedicated to learning, but we also dare not say that there are definitely no people who rely on the legacy of their parents and brothers to fool around. As for the general poor children, most of them do not have the economic ability to provide higher education or even secondary education. However, are there no talents among them who are more intelligent, more self-loving, more hardworking, and more hopeful than the children of the bourgeoisie who have received higher education? In mountain villages and farmhouses, I don't know how many of the country's capable people are floating up and down like insects! The burying of talents is not only a loss to oneself and one's family, but also a great loss to the society and the people. It is heartbreaking to talk about.

Today, the national crisis is becoming more and more urgent, and the capable people to save the country are even more insufficient. The cultivation of talents cannot be delayed. Moreover, although popular education is a major plan for establishing the country, the results are still in the future. Today, we can only quickly and rigorously implement the urgent talent education, and select and assist young people who can be the national instrument. Within ten years, the country's future may rely on this to have the opportunity to revive!

The political significance of talent education is as described above. Even from the perspective of education itself, in a country with very weak national economic strength like ours, instead of cultivating talents for national use, we are simply manufacturing a few high-level consumers or even engaging in promoting foreign goods, indirectly promoting the country's fate to danger, this is even if it is not a waste of educational efficiency, it must also bear the serious crime of being a sycophant and neglecting national affairs!

Therefore, we advocate that today's university education should not only rectify its content, but also tidy up its members. In a time of urgent need for materials, we can no longer allow a few young masters and misses to use it as a tool to muddle through and cheat diplomas. It must be known that today's higher education is the place to cultivate the most responsible cadres and talents to save the country in the current stage. One more bastard is one less arm to save the country, and one less point of strength to save the country. In this critical moment of survival, can we still perfunctorily and superficially gloss over things as before?

As for the methods of concentrating and selecting talents, I propose that among the graduating students of secondary schools in various provinces who have excellent academic performance, conduct, physique, and perseverance, conduct another concrete test (there must be more reliable standards, such as intelligence tests, physical examinations, ideological tests, etc.), select the best materials, and eliminate the next (the same is true for elementary school to secondary school). Once admitted, if there is no economic ability, give free or loan methods. This can be said to be the country's investment. In the future, as long as it can produce a Washington or other great figures who can seek welfare for the country and the people, the profits obtained will definitely be able to repay the capital and have more than enough.

I am not against popular education, on the contrary, I absolutely admit that only universal national education can place the country's fate on a rock. But at the same time, I firmly advocate that for the sake of the necessary to save the country, we must urgently engage in the selection, assistance, and education of talents!

Life

Obtaining Tobacco and Alcohol License 213

— Yang Hua

Probably the year before last, a friend Mr. X in the world of fame and fortune was honorably appointed as the chief of the ××× Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Collection Branch; lacking a "capable person" among his staff, he asked me to temporarily act as the chief of internal affairs. I am an "outsider" to taxation, and at the same time not a capable person, so I was worried and dared not take the job lightly. But on second thought: experience is learned, what does it matter? So I stepped into the tax agency and started working as a civil servant!

Before taking office, Mr. X instructed me to go to the provincial bureau to collect tobacco and alcohol licenses, tax payment certificates, etc., and told me: you can give the workers some tip money as appropriate. I thought this was a very ordinary thing, at most like receiving handouts at school, what is so rare about it!

When I arrived at the reception room of the provincial bureau, I took out the business cards of Mr. X and myself and gave them to the receptionist, saying that I wanted to meet the head of the general affairs section to collect things. There were two receptionists, one fat and one thin, and they both casually glanced at me in unison, and after a long time, hummed a sentence from their noses: "The head of the general affairs section is not easy to meet." I immediately retorted: "Because of official business, how can it be difficult to meet?" The fat one ignored me and went about his own business, only the thin one was still holding the business card, making a gesture of wanting to speak but not speaking. I felt that I had underestimated them too much at first, so I put on a smiling face and very politely told him that I was sent by Mr. X, and hoped for his help in everything. His face gradually became kind, only asking why Director X did not come in person. At that time, I was like touched the mechanism, understood their psychology, and said very generously: "I can represent Director X, and if you two help, of course I will treat you to tea. ......"

Before I could finish my words, the fat one immediately turned his face: "Easy to say, easy to say, we should serve Director X's representative, I think Director X's representative is all official business, this time going to the bureau must be very important."

I was also happy to brag at the time: "I dare not say that. But Director X and I have been friends since childhood, and I have always done better than him, this time he insisted on me going to help, it's really embarrassing! ......"

They listened even more comfortably than I said, the thin one quickly handed me a "company brand": "This cigarette is not good, please wronged the representative!"

After I finished smoking, I took out two five-yuan bills from my body and put them on the reception desk, and at the same time stated that it was just tea money, and there would be a supplement in the future. Their mouths were full of: don't! don't! While their hands touched the banknotes and stuffed them into their pockets. Finally, they said very humbly: "We two brothers originally did not dare to accept the representative's money, but if we failed your kindness, we would be impolite." Then they asked with a very sincere attitude: "How many places is the representative going to spend today?"

His question really stumped me, I didn't understand the truth in this officialdom,

Page 20

and I don't need to prepare for the expense of this receiving license. I vaguely promised that only friends who can really help can have expenses. The fat one shook his head and said: "No! No! Our provincial bureau is very difficult to let out a few directors a year, many people like us have no salary, and we can only hope for a new director, to earn a little money, and Director × is a good vacancy this time, how can they slip through?"

This remark naturally has other effects, but it makes sense, and I felt that if the two of them colluded with many people to surround me, it would be difficult to deal with. So I again stated that after the things were received, I would have to add a little tea money, and at the same time deliberately asked them how to do it. The fat one still shook his head, seemingly feeling very embarrassed: "I see it's impossible without money. You think, how can we two help?

The thin one thought for a long time before frowning and saying to the fat one: "Brother Fat, I think we two brothers will take on this matter, fortunately Representative × is not an outsider, and will always be able to take care of you and me in the future."

"You said it so easily! Take on, I don't want to take on? This is money ......"

"That's right. It's just that money is annoying!" The thin one then turned his head to me, "Representative, I think you should still take out some money, these people just want some money, you represent Director × in handling affairs, do you still begrudge this little tip? After you take over the job ... In short, we two will help you with the expenses, it's always cheaper than if you talk to them yourself. We two will help you to the end."

At this time, the two of them looked like Laurel and Hardy in my eyes, one pretending to be stupid and the other pretending to be clever. I was being played by them, and I felt so angry that I just wanted to scold them to my heart's content, but I hadn't received the things yet, and I didn't want to offend people. I thought of the story of the water-carrying worker in the yamen of the tyrant wanting to compare his size with the county magistrate, but it made me laugh secretly. I thought that I couldn't get away from the money anyway, so I took out another ten-yuan bill. With this, the two of them were happy, and immediately told me the method of dealing with it, and at the same time called the young worker in charge of the tax票 in the general affairs section to introduce me. This man's surname was Chen, and he was at most eighteen years old. I thought he was very young and thought he was a newbie who was easy to deal with, but I didn't know that he was very careful and asked me for money soon after meeting, and also said that he could not only lead me to see the head of the general affairs section, but also handle the license and tax payment certificate. He can help me to get it faster, so that no other difficulties will occur. I was really not happy to hear his long list of words, in the final analysis, it was nothing more than asking for money.

After he satisfied his request, he led me to the general affairs section. When I saw the head of the section, I took out my usual diplomatic means and explained that I was just here to collect things first, and Director × will definitely come to say goodbye tomorrow morning. After all, the head of the section was not like the receptionist, and he did not make things difficult for me, so he ordered Chen to clean up the things I should receive. But there were a lot of things, and they couldn't be sorted out for a while, so he called me to pick them up in the afternoon.

When I arrived at the reception room of the provincial bureau in the afternoon, the two fat and thin guys were really polite to me: Director Representative, they shouted so sincerely that I was really embarrassed, and they repeatedly urged Chen to clean up faster. I thought this was the price of the twenty-yuan bill, and the saying that "money can make the devil push the millstone" also has a considerable truth. But soon I encountered an important difficulty. The receiving and dispatching office, the tax section of the workers came a total of more than ten; this congratulations, that congratulations, you take cigarettes, I hand tea, so that the coffee table in front of me can not be put down. Although I was a little embarrassed in my heart, I was very calm on the surface, so I followed the method that the receptionist told me, and never showed my attitude. Whatever they talked about, I talked about, fortunately I knew a little about the truth on the road, and I didn't feel any difficulty. After prolonging like this for more than an hour, Chen ran over to call me to the general affairs section to count the things. At this time, the head of the section was not there, and the people in charge greeted me a few words, and then asked why Director × didn't come. At this time, I had gained a lot of experience and knew that I couldn't find a few good people in the tax agency, so I deliberately said that I had just called to ask Director ×, and he said that he would come over immediately to say goodbye to the colleagues in the provincial bureau. They were also half-believing. Then I quickly counted the things and asked Chen to send them out the door. At this time, the friends who had offered me tea and cigarettes were all patrolling at the door, as if preventing criminals from escaping. I shouted for the rickshaw to move things, and applied the last treasure that Da gave me: "Director × told me: There are no expenses for everyone today, and he will come tomorrow to invite everyone to drink tea. He has not said goodbye to the head of the bureau!"

At this time, the two fat and thin receptionists made a face at me again: "Please convey my regards to Director ×, we will give him congratulations and ask for tip money tomorrow!"

It was not easy to break through the siege and jump on the rickshaw, and my heart was still pounding. I thought it was not easy to enter and leave the gate of the tax agency!

Small Monograph

The Recovery of the British Economy During the Economic Panic 214

— Wu Shide

Since the outbreak of the world economic panic in 1929, the various imperialist countries have been increasingly trapped in the distress of depression. In order to alleviate their various crises, they have implemented various artificial methods in an attempt to restore the economy. However, those non-fundamental artificial methods cannot fundamentally eliminate this widespread and deeply developing disaster of economic panic, and at most can only make the situation of certain industrial sectors fairly good, and this improvement is only temporary. This situation is most obvious in the United States under Roosevelt's recovery policy; at the same time, it can also be clearly seen in the British economy in the past two years. Now, what we want to study is the temporary recovery of the British economy.

In 1932, the recovery of the British economy gradually began, and the speed of this recovery was very slow until the second half of 1934, and it can be said that it had fundamentally stopped by the end of the year. The index of the British Department of Commerce clearly shows this development process - the Department of Commerce's industrial production index (1928 equals 100); at the same time, the magazine "Economist" published such a chart (monthly average of 1924 equals 100):

1934

The first table shows that the British production index has been developing upward since 1933, but this development trend slowed down and even stopped in the second half of 1934; the latter table not only shows the same situation as the previous table, but also shows that the most important thing in the so-called recovery of the British economy is the increase in the construction and automobile production index.

However, the main reasons for the sharp increase in residential construction are, first, the low interest rate in long-term credit, and second, the low construction costs in the panic year, which is clearly shown in the table below (1924 equals 100)——

Finally, what enabled the British construction industry to recover to a certain extent was the low price of the pound.

The question of whether such a development of the construction industry can continue is entirely determined by the condition of British workers; if the lives of workers cannot be improved, if they cannot improve their housing, then the development of the construction industry in the panic year will become a temporary phenomenon and cannot continue. British politicians have been singing the song of removing slums and improving workers' housing in the election competition, but until now there is still a huge army of unemployed; these unemployed people can't even solve the problem of employment, so how can they leave the slums and how can they improve their housing? Even the employed workers, because of the low wages and poor living conditions, cannot talk about improving their housing at all. In this way, the development of the construction industry, which occupies an important position in the so-called recovery, will inevitably be temporary. In fact, from the end of last year to the present, the British construction industry has not shown a development trend.

Secondly, there is the issue of increased automobile production.

The increase in British automobile production in recent years is clearly shown in the table below——

Passenger Small Cars Large Cargo Cars

First nine months of 1929 182.347 56.458

First nine months of 1931 158.997 67.30

First nine months of 1932 171.244 61.475

From October 1932 to August 1933 208.380 59.978 From October 1933 to August 1934 241.671 78.601

What stimulated the increase in British automobile production was mainly the British government's reduction in taxes on automobile owners. But in any case, the need for automobiles is always limited, so whether British automobile production can continue to increase in the future is still a big question.

In this way, since the development trend of the construction industry and the automobile industry, which occupy a major position in the so-called recovery, cannot be optimistic, then the essence and future of the so-called recovery of the British economy is not difficult to see.

In the so-called recovery of the British economy, in addition to the construction industry and the automobile industry showing a temporary development trend, the shipbuilding industry has also improved slightly. But this improvement is not due to the improvement of the general industry, but mainly the result of the expansion of the British naval armament. At present, the economic state of the United Kingdom, on the one hand, because of many artificial reasons, although certain industrial sectors have a temporary recovery phenomenon, the panic of the general industrial sector is still continuing to develop, whether the textile industry, the coal mining industry, or the original shipbuilding industry, the excess of fixed capital is more than at any time. As for foreign trade, there have also been several improvements in recent years. According to the investigation, the export of finished industrial products in the United Kingdom has shown the following increasing trend in the past three years——

Last quarter of 1932 69.0 (unit million pounds)

Last quarter of 1933 75.2

Last quarter of 1934 81.1

However, if we compare the recent exports of the United Kingdom with the pre-panic level, the situation is very different. "Eonomist" published a comparative table of numbers on January 19 this year (unit million pounds)

What the numbers in the table above show is that although the exports of the United Kingdom have increased somewhat in recent years, they are still relatively reduced compared with the pre-panic level: This fact can be understood more clearly if we consider the recent decline in prices. As for the export of various important commodities, the situation is also very uneven. In fact, the export of cotton cloth in 1934 was somewhat reduced compared with 1933, and if compared with the pre-panic 1928, it was only a little more than half: the export of woolen fabrics is increasing, as are automobiles and pig iron; but the export of coal is now still stagnating at the very low level of two years ago.

From these actual situations, the so-called recovery of the British economy is in fact artificial, partial, and not the upward development of the general economy; moreover, due to the inability to solve the unemployment problem, the inability to improve the lives of workers, and the increasing decline in the digestive power of the domestic market, this artificial and partial so-called recovery in the United Kingdom is only temporary and cannot continue to be maintained and developed.

The Great Shanghai Scenery

Contagious Disease Hospital 215

— Ke Cong

The sun had just barely poked half its head out, and the asphalt roads on the ground were already glistening with sweat. Leaving home, one felt as if being roasted by fire; sweat oozed from the pores like asphalt on the road, and before walking even a few dozen steps, one's clothes were as soaked as a drowned chicken, clinging tightly to the skin.

After enduring half an hour of sweltering heat, what unfolded before my eyes was an environment of towering trees and tranquility, akin to a nunnery. Beneath the canopy of leaves peeked an endless stretch of black fence, tightly enclosing several new buildings that appeared to have just been completed. The national flag fluttered high on both sides of the gate. A thought lurking in my mind seemed to realize that this was the "Shanghai Municipal Contagious Disease Hospital" I was about to visit.

"This Contagious Disease Hospital was originally the 'Zhabei Public Hospital' before the 'January 28th Incident.' It was later destroyed by gunfire and taken over by the Bureau of Health, which transformed it into the current hospital. The new buildings in front were only recently completed, and considering the city's population, the wards still seem insufficient." An employee, after exchanging pleasantries with me in the reception room, pointed to a row of light yellow buildings in front and told me this.

We left the reception room and first took a walk around the open space. The hospital occupies an area of about twenty acres; it is surrounded by a black fence, and the courtyard is full of tall trees that block out the sun. The grass on the ground is like a carpet, green and boundless. Gusts of clear wind blew

Page 21

through the woods, and one felt as light as if having laid down a burden weighing hundreds of pounds.

The southern part of the hospital is an old-style building, facing the newly completed modern hospital, a rectangular structure with light yellow walls, the color of which appears even more harmonious and beautiful under the sunlight. The three buildings can accommodate approximately one hundred and forty patients. The wards are divided into first, second, and third class, with the first and second class located on the second floor, and the third class downstairs. In addition to being divided by class, the wards are also divided into pediatric wards, male and female wards, intensive care units, and other types. Other facilities such as dining rooms, nurses' offices, patient lounges, and toilets are all located within these buildings.

The living environment for patients is indeed designed to meet hygienic principles in every aspect. For example, in addition to the regular meals prepared by the "main kitchen," there is also a steam stove room in the hospital, specifically for patients to cook snacks and boil hot water at any time. For patient hygiene, in addition to the existing washrooms, a special type of bathtub is provided. This bathtub is shaped like a car, with four wheels underneath that can be freely moved. If a patient is too ill to move, the bathtub can be pushed into the room for bathing, providing much convenience to the patient. One building is divided into dozens of rooms, and the equipment in each ward has been carefully designed with artistry. The color of the walls in the rooms is the same light yellow as the outside, but the paint is applied more delicately. The furnishings include small tea tables, small desks, and electric bells, occupying very little space, leaving a large area in the middle for patients to move around. The electric lights in each room are installed in the middle of the walls, covered with white, non-glare glass panels more than a foot long and four inches wide, emitting a soft and serene light; this demonstrates the well-considered design for the patients' physical and mental health and eyesight.

The charging method for inpatients here is determined according to each individual's economic circumstances. The first-class ward costs six yuan per day, and one family member is allowed to accompany the patient, but they must pay two yuan per day for room and board. The second-class ward costs two yuan per day. The third-class ward is much cheaper, costing only thirty cents per day. The patients admitted here are mostly those suffering from the following infectious diseases: typhoid fever, scarlet fever, meningitis, cholera, dysentery, plague, diphtheria, typhus, smallpox, and others.

Their original plan was to have one building for each type of infectious disease, which is what is called an "isolation hospital." However, this plan cannot be realized for the time being due to the current shortage of buildings. Because according to their classification of medical subjects, there are nine types, which would require nine buildings, but currently only two have been completed and are habitable, while the other seven are still under construction. Therefore, to see the success of this grand plan will probably require some time.

A Week's Travel

Adventures in the Land of Ghosts 216

— Zhang Zhaoxin

In the minds of most people, "Fengdu" is generally considered a place haunted by ghosts, especially those vegetarian Buddhist women, who, upon hearing the name Fengdu, would shudder, believing it to be the land of ghosts, where everyone goes to live after death. In ancient inherited myths, it is also said that "it is a land of ghosts, and it is even rumored that it is a place where humans and ghosts live together. It is said that there is also buying and selling there. When customers buy things, the people in the shops first throw the received copper coins into a water basin prepared in advance. If the copper coins sink, the people in the shops know that they are human and give them human goods. If the copper coins float, they are not human, but a ghost, and they give them ghostly goods." Liao Shiyi also recorded such a story: "×××, a magistrate of 'Fengdu,' after taking office, heard that there was a very deep cave in the area, said to be the residence of the King of Hell. The magistrate did not believe it and went to explore it with his attendants. At first, it was very dark, but suddenly it became bright, as if illuminated by daylight. Suddenly, he saw a person dressed like the King of Hell in a drama, bowing to the magistrate and inviting him in, with a very respectful demeanor, saying, 'I have been waiting for a long time. Please take office and take over immediately.' The magistrate was terrified, repeatedly kowtowing, saying, 'My family still has an old mother. How can I do this?' The King of Hell smiled and said, 'It is the will of Heaven.' He then took out a book and pointed to it, saying, 'It has already been recorded in the book.' The magistrate looked at it and saw the book read: '××× enters the underworld alive.'" Because of this record, it has become an ironclad case, firmly believing that "Fengdu" is haunted by ghosts, even the people of Sichuan would admit it.

So, is "Fengdu" a land of ghosts? In this era of scientific advancement, this question really needs to be debunked. Last year, I went on an expedition to Sichuan and passed through "Fengdu," so I stayed there for half a day to conduct a factual investigation, hoping to dispel this question that has persisted for thousands of years.

After leaving Chongqing, the ship arrived at "Fengdu" on the second day. After going ashore and walking not far, we arrived at the so-called "Fengdu." It is a high mountain, split into two in the middle, with a distance of about three or four zhang. The cliffs are thousands of feet high, and the situation is very dangerous, as if they are about to close together. Below, more than a hundred temples are built in a dense arrangement. We walked the three or four-li-long, three-foot-wide street several times, but we never saw a single person. Looking up, we only saw a patch of sky. The sun was about to climb over the mountain, and darkness had already descended on this land of locust trees. The high mountains on both sides seemed to be on the verge of collapsing, as if they could merge at any moment. The stalagmites were shaped like various demons, seeming to seize people and eat them. Anyone other than people like us would probably be frightened and run away immediately.

Before long, it became night here. Fortunately, we had prepared flashlights in advance, which we immediately put to use. Each and every one of the temples revealed a majestic appearance, resplendent in gold. The larger ones were similar to the Jingci Temple in Hangzhou, and the smaller ones were similar to those seen on the streets of Shanghai. However, we walked a long way on the street but never saw anyone walking, except for us. At this time, I looked at my watch, which read only three o'clock.

"Hey! What time is it on your watch?" I asked my companion, "Because mine is broken."

"What?" he exclaimed, "Is it only three o'clock and already dark?" But the short hands on several companions' watches clearly pointed to three o'clock.

Regardless, we straightened our chests, turned our brains, and tried to find more materials to enrich our exploration. We walked step by step onto the stone steps in front of the temples. The doors were closed but not locked, so we pushed them open like detectives, shining our flashlights inside. Several pairs of eyes searched inside like hunting dogs, and then we walked in step by step. The four walls were covered with various wooden puppets, all gilded, and there was nothing else. At this time, we felt unbearably cold and couldn't help but shiver a little. Going further in, we saw a person with disheveled hair, looking just like a ghost. If there were ghosts, I believe that the appearance of ghosts must be similar to his. We steadied our minds and looked at him. We saw his swarthy face set off by his disheveled long hair, wearing thick cotton clothes, barefoot, wearing a pair of straw sandals, with ten fingers as thick as carrots. There were also several bald guys next to him, all with sturdy bodies. We looked carefully for a while and then believed that these were all people, because if they were ghosts, they should have immediately dodged and disappeared when they saw us. They also looked at us with surprised eyes.

"Are you here to play?" An older man stood up to greet us, speaking in a pure Sichuan Xiajiang dialect.

"Yes! We are here to play," we replied, "Are you all from here?"

He nodded, invited us to sit down, and then I began to use conversation to find the materials we needed.

"Are there ghosts here?" I asked with a smile.

"Ghosts, we haven't seen them, but the people here all believe that there are, so we live in the temples all year round. Every morning when we get up, we all go to a small temple on the mountain to burn incense. The Bodhisattva there is called Xiaorenzi, and he is really effective! If you don't go to burn incense, then you can forget about having a peaceful day today. When you fall asleep, ghosts and demons will come to surround you. When you cook rice, the rice will turn into feces. Last time, some guests came to play, and they tried it on the spot. Clearly, they put in white rice, but after cooking for a while, when they lifted the pot lid, there was no trace of white rice in the pot, it had all turned into feces!"

We smiled and took out bread to eat, but none of it changed flavor.

"Why does it get dark at three o'clock?"

"Here, it doesn't get light until eleven o'clock in the morning, and it gets dark at three o'clock in the afternoon. There are only four hours of daylight, and the rest is darkness."

"How many families are there here?"

"There are about a hundred families, with five or six hundred people. This place has now been changed to 'Fengdu' County, and there is a county magistrate and a public security bureau, just like outside."

"So, is the county magistrate here?"

"No, we have only heard that there is a county magistrate, but we have never seen him. It is said that the county magistrate is because it is too hard, and he only takes the name, and never comes here in person. There are a dozen policemen, who live the same way as we do, except that they ask us for money and grain every year."

"Then do you also farm?"

"Of course, we do. Our fields are all on the mountains, and the harvest is good every year. Most of what is produced here is corn, which is shipped to Chongqing every year to sell. After selling it, we buy foreign cloth back to make clothes, and other miscellaneous items are also bought from there, but the road is too inconvenient! So it's hard to go there a few times a year."

"How long have you been living in 'Fengdu'? Why do you live in the temples?"

"We don't know! I only know that my father lived here, and I don't understand anything else!"

"Where do the high mountains separate here, and where do they come together again?"

"Further on is Wushan, where they come together."

It was getting late, so we smiled and recited the lines "Having seen the sea, other waters are hard to call water; having seen Wushan, other clouds are not clouds," and then withdrew from the remote place, and retraced our steps back.

Opinions

The Sin of a Single Strike 217

— Xin Zi

On July 17th, a certain publication carried a news item about a widow who remarried and injured her husband, the gist of which was that "Huang Hengbi already had a wife, and seventeen years ago, due to his work at the Chongming Post Office, he was on a long-distance assignment, separated by distant mountains and rivers. Therefore, he did not bring his family with him. Being alone in a foreign land with plenty of leisure time, he sought out a beautiful woman to relieve his loneliness. It happened that Xia Wu was newly widowed and not tolerated by her in-laws, so Huang purchased her marriage certificate from the Xia family for a price of one hundred and thirty yuan and built a golden house for her. Later, Huang was transferred back to the General Post Office, and the woman remained on Chongming Island. Huang initially provided for Wu's household expenses from time to time, but later, due to the larger expenses in Shanghai, he could not provide as generously as before. After three years, the woman traced him to Shanghai, made things difficult for him, and eventually went to his office to make trouble, injuring Huang with a wine bottle." The reporter of this publication used the words "innately shrewish" in the headline to judge the remarried widow, while Huang Hengbi seemed to have been forgiven in the reporter's writing.

In the current society where men still dominate everything, it is to be expected that the case should receive such an evaluation. Men can go anywhere to find a machine for sexual release for their own enjoyment, so like Huang Hengbi, even in the current system of monogamy, he can build a golden house, taking advantage of a person's family discord and economic distress to become a guest in their house. Ms. Jun Hui spoke most incisively about this illegal marriage phenomenon in her article "Modern Marriage and Divorce": "From the perspective of our women, this kind of union is completely sacrificing women's human rights to satisfy men's sexual life, which is extremely immoral. Men who live as concubines often have their legal wives at home, and when they are away from home due to their work, they use money, power, and other deceptive methods to lure women into illegal cohabitation.

Continued on page 5

Page 22

Page 23

But when he gets tired of it, he discards them like worn-out shoes." For Huang Hengbi's immoral behavior, we should first condemn him for the sake of justice, but what we see in public opinion is the condemnation of the remarried "widow" for being "innately shrewish," and not the condemnation of Huang Hengbi for "trampling on women," which is very unfair!

The monogamous marriage system already has clear provisions in our grand laws, but what we see in the social phenomenon is that, in addition to one wife, men still have ways to engage in various polygamous practices behind the name of "one wife." Prostitution and cohabitation, are these not enough to illustrate the actual existence of polygamy? In the current capitalist society dominated by commodity economy, the concept of chastity is still one-sidedly existent, and the monogamous system is still nothing more than a means to bind women's chastity!

Huang Hengbi treated both his legal wife and Wu as consistently as "hotel-style sexual transaction" objects. He himself could be content wherever he was, whether on Chongming Island or in Shanghai, he could get sexual satisfaction. In the continuation of the sexual transaction relationship, he naturally used the supply of money as the only means to deceive the other party. Once the sexual transaction was interrupted (such as after Huang left Chongming), he even abandoned the disguise of monetary support! Wu has no status in law. After being abandoned by Huang, can she get fair legal relief? She can't. How will she cope? In general feudal women, perhaps they would sob and swallow their tears and hang themselves or take poison to find relief? This is naturally the behavior of the weak, but our remarried widow still has the courage to use a wine bottle to strike the "woman trampling" Huang Hengbi because of her "innate shrewishness." Let us imagine how much resentment and humiliation accumulated in the hearts of women for thousands of years is contained in this strike! However, this poor widow was finally judged with the crime of being "innately shrewish"!

Special Report

Overseas Chinese Around the World (4) 218

— Zhong Minyi

(2) Overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia

Southeast Asia includes the Malay Peninsula, Indochina, and the East Indies. Now, we will describe the situation of overseas Chinese in these places separately.

Thailand. Thailand is located between French Indochina and British Malaya, on the Indochina Peninsula in Southeast Asia. As early as the Northern and Southern Dynasties, Thailand sent envoys to pay tribute to China. Its relationship with China must have been even more ancient. Up to now, there are more than three million overseas Chinese in Thailand, accounting for more than a quarter of the total population of Thailand and a third of the total number of overseas Chinese in the world. The status of overseas Chinese in Thailand in the world of overseas Chinese, and the relationship between overseas Chinese and the country of Thailand can be seen from this.

Most of the overseas Chinese in Thailand come from Guangdong and Fujian. They mostly engage in industry and commerce here, and they occupy a very important position in the Thai economy. Almost all of Thailand's important industries and businesses are in their hands. As we all know, the rice and mining industries are the main industries of Thailand, but according to a survey in 1919, in Bangkok alone, there were a total of 67 large rice mills, of which 56 were owned by Chinese. In addition, industries such as sugar manufacturing, timber, and pawnshops are also operated by overseas Chinese. If we only talk about the economic aspect, Thailand can be said to be the Thailand of overseas Chinese.

However, the colonial world of a country cannot continue to develop only by relying on the economic power and hard work of its expatriates. Therefore, the colonial policies of many modern independent countries are implemented under the political power of the state. China is a backward semi-colonial country, and it has never had a definite immigration policy, let alone how to help overseas Chinese scattered around the world. Although overseas Chinese in Thailand have such great power, China and Thailand have not yet established formal diplomatic relations. Therefore, the more the overseas Chinese develop in Thailand, the more they will be suppressed and excluded by the Thai government and unable to cope. In recent years, the Thai government has repeatedly promulgated immigration laws, repeatedly increasing the import tax for Chinese people to limit Chinese imports. What is even worse is the recent crackdown on overseas Chinese schools and the implementation of compulsory education to assimilate our compatriots, in the hope of assimilating our three million overseas Chinese into Thais and taking over our huge property. According to reports, in the past year alone, more than 70 overseas Chinese schools were closed by the Thai government. The industries and businesses operated by overseas Chinese are especially subject to heavy taxation, making it impossible for them to maintain themselves. Overseas Chinese are also prohibited and restricted from remitting money back home. In October of the year before last, a major tragedy of Thai police slaughtering overseas Chinese occurred in southern Thailand, killing dozens of people. Recently, our compatriots have been oppressed and returned in batches… All these are concrete manifestations of the Thai government's oppression of overseas Chinese. At present, the anti-Chinese movement in Thailand is still increasing. If we do not hurry up and find ways to deal with it, I am afraid that the three million overseas Chinese in Thailand will not be able to stand on their feet!

Student in Love 220

The pitiable fellow is a student at the Love School, stupid in nature, without a match, truly detrimental to the school's reputation, and is again protected by his classmates, who bully him for his loneliness. Soon, he obtains the affection of the daughter of the school's imprisoned, the girl is also alone, so he goes to pair with her. However, the principal, because his daughter does not wish to match with the stupid man, obstructs them. Thereupon, the masses know that he has been fooled, and rise up in difficulty. The principal is unable to respond, and is then expelled. The students, because the national crisis is pressing, mutually accompany each other to join the military, taking a free bus, together going to the path of light.

It has been a long time since Holland's Ai Luan has had her work seen. This time, Universal Pictures of the United States bought a good script and designated the great director Code Naumen and famous actors such as Raymond Milland, Henry O'Neill, Katherine Alisede, and child star Bebe Qisi. It can be called a perfect combination of talents, making the protagonist Sharon Ai Luan able to display her expressive genius. As for the photography, recording, background, and dialogue, the various technical excellences are secondary matters. At the same time, Universal's full-color artistic music short "Song of Welcoming Spring" will also be shown, and the latest dance step "Groller Clou dland" will be introduced. The four new films being produced by Lianhua, "Family Ethics," "Little Angel," "Four Sisters," and "Wild Geese Descending on the Cold River," are about to be completed. The titles have not yet been decided. All will begin filming in mid-August.
